  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bb6fffba-6128-4134-a9a0-df8ab323de9a'
      });
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer6438362464850062592">Two novellas set in the world of Kiera Cass's #1 <em>New York Times</em> bestselling Selection series are now available in print for the first time. <em>The Prince</em> and <em>The Guard</em> both offer captivating views into the hearts and minds of the two men fighting to win America Singer's love. This collection also features exclusive bonus content, including a sneak peek at <em>The One</em>, the eagerly</span>
  <span id="freeText6438362464850062592" style="display:none">Two novellas set in the world of Kiera Cass's #1 <em>New York Times</em> bestselling Selection series are now available in print for the first time. <em>The Prince</em> and <em>The Guard</em> both offer captivating views into the hearts and minds of the two men fighting to win America Singer's love. This collection also features exclusive bonus content, including a sneak peek at <em>The One</em>, the eagerly anticipated third novel in the Selection series.<br /><br />Before America arrived at the palace to compete in the Selection, there was another girl in Prince Maxon's life. <em>The Prince</em> opens the week before the Selection begins and follows Maxon through the first day of the competition.<br /><br />Raised as a Six, Aspen Leger never dreamed that he would find himself living in the palace as a member of the royal guard. In <em>The Guard</em>, readers get an inside look at Aspen's life within the palace walls—and the truth about a guard's world that America will never know.</span>

<div id="review_2617260869" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2617260869" />
    <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52207144"><img alt="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568965358p2/52207144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2617260869?book_show_action=true">Dec 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ" href="/user/show/52207144">♥ℂĦℝΪՖƬΪℕÅ</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=novellas">novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=dystopia-and-utopian">dystopia-and-utopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52207144?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2617260869" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7323767448737488959">Both of these novellas were fast passed and really easy to read. They were not the best but still, I'm very happy I took the time to read them. I recommend reading this especially fans of <i>The Selection</i> series because it does give some good insights :) <br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539158879i/26427386._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><b>The Prince:</b> ★★★✰✰<br/><br/><i>“There was something about her.. Even the way she didn't like me drew me in, and I couldn't help but smile.”</i><br/><br/>This one was just alright. I didn't love it but I can't say I hated it either. It's written in Prince Maxon's POV which was</span>
  <span id="freeText7323767448737488959" style="display:none">Both of these novellas were fast passed and really easy to read. They were not the best but still, I'm very happy I took the time to read them. I recommend reading this especially fans of <i>The Selection</i> series because it does give some good insights :) <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1539158879i/26427386._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The Prince:</b> ★★★✰✰<br><br><i>“There was something about her.. Even the way she didn't like me drew me in, and I couldn't help but smile.”</i><br><br>This one was just alright. I didn't love it but I can't say I hated it either. It's written in Prince Maxon's POV which was initially what drew me to want to read it in the first place. It takes place a couple of weeks before <i>The Selection</i> which just so happens to be on his 19th birthday. I really enjoyed the first few chapters. The ones that took place before. It was nice seeing all the work that went into the preparations for the 'lottery' that really wasn't a lottery at all! And seeing it all through Maxson's eyes. It was wonderful to be inside his head, to see his fears and doubts throughout the whole prosses and what his expectations were going into it and whether or not if he'd find love in the end. I have loved Maxon from day one and this just helped solidify it even more. He's charming, sweet, passionate, a bit sheltered and he generally cares about The Selection and each one of the girls. I also enjoyed having his thoughts on the girls as well. Especially the one he has about America :) Maxon is so damn easy to love! The last couple of chapters were retellings of Maxon and America's first couple encounters in <i>The Selection</i> just through Maxon instead. And they were pretty boring because of it. <br> <br>Illustration of Maxon &amp; What I picture he'd look like.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544255458i/26713496.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>
  <i>“If she were (looking into my eyes), she’d have seen how absolutely floored I was the first time I finally, truly saw her. The clouds moved at just the right moment, fully lighting her face by the moon. She was dazzlingly beautiful. Underneath thick lashes were eyes blue as ice, something cool to balance out the flames in her hair. I felt a strange flutter in my chest, like the glow of a fireplace or the warmth of the afternoon. It stayed there for a moment, playing with my pulse.”</i>
</b><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1543275640i/26652408._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The Guard:</b> ★★★✰✰<br><br><i>“Accepting help is its own kind of strength”</i><br><br><i>The Guard</i> was... Well, it was just an okay read I guess. I get a bit bored when there are repeat scenes from previous books. And if I'm being honest Aspen's POV really didn't add that much to the story which is sad because I was looking most forward to his. I guess I was looking for something more and sadly this just didn't deliver. And even though I distaste repeated scenes (scenes from <i>The Elite</i>) it was still nice getting a look into his thoughts and feelings and his desires. Aspens POV gives us insight into King Clarkson's nature, motivations, manipulative ways, and his cruelty. It was also nice getting to see the relationship's form between him and America's maids Anne, Marry and Lucy and the respect they have for him and the love they have for America. It was nice seeing Aspen's camaraderie with the other guards, especially with Avery and Tanner. Also, I enjoyed the couple scenes between Aspen and the old man who works in the stables. The old man gives some pretty good advice too :) My rating for this book has nothing to do with my liking or not liking Aspen. It's solely based on the content and the entertainment factor which was very low in my opinion. And... For the record, I have always loved Aspen ever since the first book! Not necessarily with America but because his dedication to America remains steadfast throughout EVERYTHING and he's caring, sweet and all around a wonderful person. <br><br>Illustration of Aspen &amp; What I picture he'd look like.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1544243935i/26712472.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“I pushed my lips to hers, locking her to me with a hand knotted into her hair. Stupid. So, so stupid. But right in a thousand ways. It felt like an eternity had passed since we'd kissed this deeply, but we fell into it so easily.”</i><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1543991333ra/26692646.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>“You’re the only thing I’ve ever wanted to fight for.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7323767448737488959" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18225321580709505260">So, my obsession with The Selection continues. It took me so long to find this book for sale in brazil, but FOUND IT! <br/>Okay, to start with, i have to say im a little sad. I honestly don't like Aspen, but he takes like 70% of the book hahah. Still, it was good to see everything from his perspective.<br/><br/>The Prince:<br/>I love how since the beginning he kind of knew America was the one.   <span id="freeText18225321580709505260" style="display:none">So, my obsession with The Selection continues. It took me so long to find this book for sale in brazil, but FOUND IT! <br />Okay, to start with, i have to say im a little sad. I honestly don't like Aspen, but he takes like 70% of the book hahah. Still, it was good to see everything from his perspective.<br /><br />The Prince:<br />I love how since the beginning he kind of knew America was the one. I don't know, but just seeing how he felt towards King Clarkson, and the Selection, gave him a more "I'm not just a prince, im human" look. Because before, on the selection books (not the novelas) its kind of like Maxon is untouchable, like he can get through anything. But then, you see he didn't want the selection, he didn't have freedom, he was just a weak boy trying to chose a wife when he didn't know the first thing about girls. But yet he was like heaven. <br /><br />The Guard:<br />I don't like Aspen, haven't liked him since he became a Guard. And on the guard, i have only disliked him more. I mean he tried to push America down "Do you think I could do it? If i became a princess?" and HE SAYS NO! Like i get it you're in love, and all, but you are a 6!!!! Maxon is a 1!!! I mean not only that, Aspen puts his interests first, and wants America to himself. America loved both Maxon AND Aspen, and he tried to degrade Maxon. </span>

<div id="review_1009782038" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1009782038" />
    <a title="Kristina Horner" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3070540-kristina-horner"><img alt="Kristina Horner" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425746408p2/3070540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1009782038?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristina Horner" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristina Horner" href="/user/show/3070540-kristina-horner">Kristina Horner</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3070540-kristina-horner?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3070540-kristina-horner?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1009782038" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1530039662697173537">To be perfectly honest, I really don't think this book added anything to the Selection Series. <br/>It mostly rehashed scenes we've already experienced (but from the male's point of view, whoop-de-do) so it felt a little tedious, basically reliving conversations we've already seen. I was really hoping for backstory on these guys, or things going on with them that we couldn't see from America's point of view. Not the case.<br/><br/>Maxon's just made him look naive and a little pathetic - it was cheesy, poorly w</span>
  <span id="freeText1530039662697173537" style="display:none">To be perfectly honest, I really don't think this book added anything to the Selection Series. <br />It mostly rehashed scenes we've already experienced (but from the male's point of view, whoop-de-do) so it felt a little tedious, basically reliving conversations we've already seen. I was really hoping for backstory on these guys, or things going on with them that we couldn't see from America's point of view. Not the case.<br /><br />Maxon's just made him look naive and a little pathetic - it was cheesy, poorly written, and the things Clarkson said to him were just so laughable outlandish for the sake of driving home that fact that he's a villain... I just couldn't take it seriously.<br /><br />Aspen's was even worse - insufferable, self-righteous, and simply delusional. Telling America over and over again that Maxon's affection for him isn't real, feeling so sure she's going to choose him... I was even MORE glad she doesn't, after reading this.<br /><br />It was sloppy, rushed, and a wholly unnecessary book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1530039662697173537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46201957-guiana?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46201957-guiana?shelf=before-2020-ends">before-2020-ends</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1989315428" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2683381882767604628">» 3.5 stars<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <blockquote>
    <b>
      <i>"Eh. Everything doesn't seem like anything when you love someone. Especially when you're young."</i>
    </b>
  </blockquote>
</blockquote><br/>disclaimer: the last <i>The Selection</i> book I read—<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22918050.The_Heir__The_Selection___4_' title='The Heir (The Selection, #4) by Kiera Cass' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Heir</a>—was three years ago so my memory of the series is stilted and nearly nonexistent, and this particular review doesn't exactly reflect any of those others with the same knowledge, except that I was largely and still am, as this book proves, biasedly Maxon > Aspen. not an attack, it's just that <i>Maxon</i>, y'know?<br/><br/><b>warnin</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2683381882767604628" style="display:none">» 3.5 stars<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <blockquote>
    <b>
      <i>"Eh. Everything doesn't seem like anything when you love someone. Especially when you're young."</i>
    </b>
  </blockquote>
</blockquote><br />disclaimer: the last <i>The Selection</i> book I read—<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22918050.The_Heir__The_Selection___4_" title="The Heir (The Selection, #4) by Kiera Cass" rel="nofollow noopener">The Heir</a>—was three years ago so my memory of the series is stilted and nearly nonexistent, and this particular review doesn't exactly reflect any of those others with the same knowledge, except that I was largely and still am, as this book proves, biasedly Maxon &gt; Aspen. not an attack, it's just that <i>Maxon</i>, y'know?<br /><br /><b>warning! rant ahead!</b><br /><br />I wanted to enjoy all of this book, I really did. but, more than half was Aspen, and I've decided (again) that I have some problems with his character. as mentioned, I don't mean to attack him or those who think there is nothing wrong with his quite hypocritical ways. it was just hard for me to feel for him as a whole, even seeing things from his perspective, because the irrationality of his actions from the beginning of the series has not been forgotten by my ire the least bit since then. if anything, my complete disbelief about that skyrocketed after reading this when I personally felt he was whining about something that, ultimately, was done by his hands, barely acknowledging and for the most part pretending that some outer, higher force has separated him from the girl he loves when really...he could just look at a mirror and find the answer. also, I was bothered throughout when he'd claim America as his as if it was that simple after all those things? that <i>he</i> propelled into action, mind you? I know it seems as if I'm ranting because I'm all swoony and heart-eyes for Maxon, which I <i>am</i> all swoony and heart-eyes for Maxon, but what I feel for Aspen's character itself is entirely separate from that bias. it would physically hurt me to read the same set of traits on another character all the same.<br /><br />I could have done without <i>The Guard</i>, yes, but it provided insight. I'll refrain from commenting on <i>The Prince</i> much except that it was lovely and actually helped me understand the feelings and see the growth of a character. plus, the prince himself.<br /><br />I'd have very different ratings of the two novellas if they were separate. as it is, I'm torn between rating it higher or lower, just as I feel for one story then the other. I'm relenting to a compromise of 3.5 stars rounded to 4 in the Goodreads system, but my aggressive opinions not be forgotten! I've never had anything carry the rating of a book more than <i>The Prince</i>, this one novella saving it all.</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3215604664460156643" style="display:none">This was a nice addition to the story, because we can see the thoughts of Maxon and Aspen, however, it was kinda boring as I've already read about these events in America's point of view. As I obviously knew what was gonna happen, it did feel like a re-read, and for me it was too soon after reading the trilogy, so it wasn't really exciting.<br />I remember hating Aspen when reading the trilogy, but now I just didn't. I didn't love Maxon and didn't hate Aspen, just had no feelings for the characters at all. <br />I liked the Q&amp;A with the author at the end, I found that interesting, I usually like reading about where a certain idea comes from, and how someone makes it into a story. How they come up with names, and in what order they write the book. Idk. I just find these stuff interesting, I know... I'm weird. But I'm glad that it was included.<br /></span>

<div id="review_2833296170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2833296170" />
    <a title="Paula  Phillips" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1969584-paula-phillips"><img alt="Paula  Phillips" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574564336p2/1969584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2833296170?book_show_action=true">May 25, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Paula  Phillips" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Paula  Phillips" href="/user/show/1969584-paula-phillips">Paula  Phillips</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2833296170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7314699383180261689"><br/>This was a series when it was released as ARCS, I read all three books as advanced review copies and loved it to bits. Then her daughter's series was released, and I didn't enjoy it as I found her daughter to be a spoilt brat, and it put a damper on this series for as I all of a sudden no longer wanted to read the short stories. Now on medical leave, I had lots of time on my hand and decided to go back and read some of my older reads, which included The Prince and The Guard. As soon as I opened </span>
  <span id="freeText7314699383180261689" style="display:none"><br />This was a series when it was released as ARCS, I read all three books as advanced review copies and loved it to bits. Then her daughter's series was released, and I didn't enjoy it as I found her daughter to be a spoilt brat, and it put a damper on this series for as I all of a sudden no longer wanted to read the short stories. Now on medical leave, I had lots of time on my hand and decided to go back and read some of my older reads, which included The Prince and The Guard. As soon as I opened the book and started reading, I was transported back into the world of America Singer. This time, however, from Maxon's POV and Aspen's POVs. In The Prince, we read about Maxon's first love which started as a friendship but he didn't have long-lasting feelings for her, and because of this The Selection was called. We read the lead-up to the selection, from the culling of the girls and his first meetings with them all and how he came to fall head over heels for America, a feeling he had never felt before. The second story was The Guard which tells the story of Aspen who loves America and thought that she would be his HEA , Aspen knows about the rebels and gets a job at the Palace to help protect America but soon the pair of them will realize the dangers if they were caught fraternizing as they witness terrible events to those accused of affairs and treason. In this book, Aspen and America come to realize that they can never love one another and that to survive, they must accept their fates and move on. The Selection Stories is the perfect companion read for fans of Kiera Cass's The Selection.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7314699383180261689" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15328603889704720862">I loved getting glimpses of Maxon and Aspen's POV.   <span id="freeText15328603889704720862" style="display:none">I loved getting glimpses of Maxon and Aspen's POV. I especially loved getting a little more insight into what was going on with them during books 1 &amp; 2, and in some ways, try to sort out which one I felt would be a more ideal match for America. Before reading Aspen's novella (The Guard, book #2.5), I was completely on board for Team Maxon. Now, after reading it, I'm still...Team Maxon, but I have feels for Aspen. hahaha<br /><br />All I know is, I sure hope that America ends up with Maxon, and that Aspen can find his happiness elsewhere. I love him so much as a character, but just not the one for her. <br /><br />PS, the sneak peek of book 3 that's at the end: TOTALLY WORTH READING. I hate teasers and stuff, but I couldn't resist reading it! I can't freaking wait for The One!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('d63vA6+RvRy62pk/jRUrPPWNxYcv7qXjIhfOxUh3JjgNMjq/Cz/39AgvXf5Fahm+r56osdh9SACykifoRxLL/Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }
